        </sup>
       </td>
       <td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">
        11.7%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:left">
        Source:
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-histpop_27-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-histpop-27">
          [25]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2010_91-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Census2010-91">
          [87]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Note:
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
         <a href="#cite_note-93">
          [e]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">
       U.S. Census Bureau
      </a>
      estimates that the District's population was 672,228 on July 1, 2015, an 11.7% increase since the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
       2010 United States Census
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The increase continues a growth trend since 2000, following a half-century of population decline.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The city was the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">
       24th most populous place
      </a>
      in the United States as of 2010
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington,_D.C.&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to data from 2010, commuters from the suburbs increase the District's daytime population to over one million people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        [91]
       </a>
      </sup>
      If the District were a state it would rank
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">
       49th in population
      </a>
      , ahead of
      <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">
       Vermont
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">
       Wyoming
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_1-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2046" data-file-width="3126" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG/220px-4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG/330px-4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG/440px-4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:4_-_7_Logan_Circle.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Row houses on
        <a href="/wiki/Logan_Circle,_Washington,_D.C." title="Logan Circle, Washington, D.C.">
         Logan Circle
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area">
       Washington Metropolitan Area
      </a>
      , which includes the District and surrounding suburbs, is the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
       seventh-largest
      </a>
      metropolitan area in the United States with an estimated 6 million residents in 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MetroPop_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-MetroPop-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      When the Washington area is included with
      <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">
       Baltimore
      </a>
      and its suburbs, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Baltimore–Washington Metropolitan Area">
       Baltimore–Washington Metropolitan Area
      </a>
      had a population exceeding 9.5 million residents in 2014, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Combined_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Combined Statistical Areas">
       fourth-largest
      </a>
      combined statistical area in the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to 2015 Census Bureau data, the population of Washington, D.C. was 48.3% Black or African American, 44.1% White (36.1% non-Hispanic White), 4.2%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">
       Asian
      </a>
      , 0.6% American Indian or Alaska Native, and 0.2% Native Hawaiian or Other Pacific Islander. Individuals from two or more races made up 2.7% of the population. Hispanics of any race made up 10.6% of the District's population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Washington has had a
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._cities_with_large_African-American_populations" title="List of U.S. cities with large African-American populations">
       significant African American population
      </a>
      since the city's foundation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      African American residents composed about 30% of the District's total population between 1800 and 1940.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-histpop_27-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-histpop-27">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The black population reached a peak of 70% by 1970, but has since steadily declined due to many African Americans moving to the surrounding suburbs. Partly as a result of
      <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">
       gentrification
      </a>
      , there was a 31.4% increase in the non-Hispanic white population and an 11.5% decrease in the black population between 2000 and 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demshift_100-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-demshift-100">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      About 17% of D.C. residents were age 18 or younger in 2010; lower than the U.S. average of 24%. However, at 34 years old, the District had the lowest median age compared to the 50 states.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2010
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington,_D.C.&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , there were an estimated 81,734
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">
       immigrants
      </a>
      living in Washington, D.C.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCsocial_102-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DCsocial-102">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Major sources of immigration include
      <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
       El Salvador
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">
       Vietnam
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopia
      </a>
      , with a concentration of Salvadorans in the
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pleasant,_Washington,_D.C." title="Mount Pleasant, Washington, D.C.">
       Mount Pleasant
      </a>
      neighborhood.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Researchers found that there were 4,822 same-sex couples in the District of Columbia in 2010; about 2% of total households.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Legislation
      <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_District_of_Columbia" title="Same-sex marriage in the District of Columbia">
       authorizing same-sex marriage
      </a>
      passed in 2009 and the District began issuing marriage licenses to same-sex couples in March 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A 2007 report found that about one-third of District residents were
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Functionally_illiterate" title="Functionally illiterate">
       functionally illiterate
      </a>
      , compared to a national rate of about one in five. This is attributed in part to immigrants who are not proficient in English.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2011
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington,_D.C.&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , 85% of D.C. residents age 5 and older spoke English at home as a primary language.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Half of residents had at least a four-year college degree in 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCsocial_102-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DCsocial-102">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      D.C. residents had a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/States_of_the_United_States_of_America_by_income" title="States of the United States of America by income">
       personal income per capita
      </a>
      of $55,755; higher than any of the 50 states.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, 19% of residents were below the poverty level in 2005, higher than any state except
      <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">
       Mississippi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Of the District's population, 17% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">
       Baptist
      </a>
      , 13% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
       Catholic
      </a>
      , 6% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">
       Evangelical Protestant
      </a>
      , 4% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist">
       Methodist
      </a>
      , 3% is
      <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">
       Episcopalian
      </a>
      /
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">
       Anglican
      </a>
      , 3% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
       Jewish
      </a>
      , 2% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">
       Eastern Orthodox
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
       Pentecostal
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">
       Buddhist
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">
       Adventist
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">
       Lutheran
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
       Muslim
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presbyterian" title="Presbyterian">
       Presbyterian
      </a>
      , 1% is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon">
       Mormon
      </a>
      , and 1% is
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
       Hindu
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        [f]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Over 90% of D.C. residents have health insurance coverage, the second-highest rate in the nation. This is due in part to city programs that help provide insurance to low-income individuals who do not qualify for other types of coverage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A 2009 report found that at least 3% of District residents have HIV or AIDS, which the
      <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">
       Centers for Disease Control and Prevention
      </a>
      (CDC) characterizes as a "generalized and severe" epidemic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
       Crime
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Crime in Washington, D.C.">
       Crime in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Crime in Washington, D.C., is concentrated in areas associated with poverty, drug abuse, and gangs. A 2010 study found that 5% of city blocks accounted for over one-quarter of the District's total crime.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCPI_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DCPI-114">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The more affluent neighborhoods of Northwest Washington are typically safe, but reports of violent crime increase in poorer neighborhoods generally concentrated in the eastern portion of the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DCPI_114-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DCPI-114">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Approximately 60,000 residents are ex-convicts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Washington was often described as the "murder capital" of the United States during the early 1990s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The number of murders peaked in 1991 at 479, but the level of violence then began to decline significantly.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 2012, Washington's annual murder count had dropped to 88, the lowest total since 1961.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        [112]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The murder rate has risen since that historic low, and as of December 11, 2015, the District's homicide total for the year stands at 154, a 58.8% increase over the same period in 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is still a murder rate of almost half that of the early 2000s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many neighborhoods such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_Heights,_Washington,_D.C." title="Columbia Heights, Washington, D.C.">
       Columbia Heights
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Logan_Circle,_Washington,_D.C." title="Logan Circle, Washington, D.C.">
       Logan Circle
      </a>
      are becoming safer and vibrant. However, incidents of robberies and thefts have remained higher in these areas because of increased nightlife activity and greater numbers of affluent residents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-klein_121-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-klein-121">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Even still, citywide reports of both property and violent crimes have declined by nearly half since their most recent highs in the mid-1990s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 26, 2008, the Supreme Court of the United States held in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_v._Heller" title="District of Columbia v. Heller">
        District of Columbia v. Heller
       </a>
      </i>
      that the city's 1976
      <a href="/wiki/Firearms_Control_Regulations_Act_of_1975" title="Firearms Control Regulations Act of 1975">
       handgun ban
      </a>
      violated the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Second Amendment to the United States Constitution">
       Second Amendment
      </a>
      right to gun ownership.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the ruling does not prohibit all forms of gun control; laws requiring firearm registration remain in place, as does the city's assault weapon ban.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition to the District's own
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Department_of_the_District_of_Columbia" title="Metropolitan Police Department of the District of Columbia">
       Metropolitan Police Department
      </a>
      , many
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_law_enforcement_in_the_United_States" title="Federal law enforcement in the United States">
       federal law enforcement agencies
      </a>
      have jurisdiction in the city as well; most visibly the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Park_Police" title="U.S. Park Police">
       U.S. Park Police
      </a>
      , founded in 1791.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Companies_based_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Category:Companies based in Washington, D.C.">
       Category:Companies based in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Non-profit_organizations_based_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Category:Non-profit organizations based in Washington, D.C.">
       Category:Non-profit organizations based in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Washington has a growing, diversified economy with an increasing percentage of professional and business service jobs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The gross state product of the District in 2010 was $103.3 billion, which would rank it No. 34 compared to the 50 states.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The gross product of the Washington Metropolitan Area was $425 billion in 2010, making it the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_United_States_by_GMP" title="List of metropolitan areas in the United States by GMP">
       fourth-largest metropolitan economy
      </a>
      in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of June 2011, the Washington Metropolitan Area had an unemployment rate of 6.2%; the second-lowest rate among the 49
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
       largest metro areas
      </a>
      in the nation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The District of Columbia itself had an unemployment rate of 9.8% during the same time period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG">
        <img alt="A wide, one story red brick building with a sloping black roof behind numerous white-topped tents selling assorted wares." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1893" data-file-width="3628" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG/220px-Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG/330px-Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG/440px-Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Market_-_southeast_corner.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Market,_Washington,_D.C." title="Eastern Market, Washington, D.C.">
         Eastern Market
        </a>
        on Capitol Hill houses food vendors and artisan stalls.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2012, the federal government accounted for about 29% of the jobs in Washington, D.C.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fedjobs_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fedjobs-131">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is thought to immunize Washington to national economic downturns because the federal government continues operations even during recessions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many organizations such as law firms, independent contractors (both defense and civilian), non-profit organizations, lobbying firms, trade unions, industry trade groups, and professional associations have their headquarters in or near D.C. to be close to the federal government.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kstreet_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-kstreet-83">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Tourism is Washington's second largest industry. Approximately 18.9 million visitors contributed an estimated $4.8 billion to the local economy in 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourism2012_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tourism2012-133">
        [127]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The District also hosts nearly 200 foreign embassies and international organizations such as the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">
       World Bank
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
       International Monetary Fund (IMF)
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
       Organization of American States
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">
       Inter-American Development Bank
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Health_Organization" title="Pan American Health Organization">
       Pan American Health Organization
      </a>
      . In 2008, the foreign
      <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_corps" title="Diplomatic corps">
       diplomatic corps
      </a>
      in Washington employed about 10,000 people and contributed an estimated $400 million annually to the local economy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-embassies_84-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-embassies-84">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The District has growing industries not directly related to government, especially in the areas of education, finance, public policy, and scientific research.
      <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">
       Georgetown University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_University" title="George Washington University">
       George Washington University
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Hospital_Center" title="Washington Hospital Center">
       Washington Hospital Center
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_National_Medical_Center" title="Children's National Medical Center">
       Children's National Medical Center
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Howard_University" title="Howard University">
       Howard University
      </a>
      are the top five non-government-related employers in the city as of 2009
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington,_D.C.&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to statistics compiled in 2011, four of the
      <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
       largest 500 companies
      </a>
      in the country were headquartered in the District.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        [129]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_sites_and_museums">
       Historic sites and museums
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Landmarks_in_Washington,_D.C." title="List of National Historic Landmarks in Washington, D.C.">
       List of National Historic Landmarks in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
      ;
      <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_Washington,_D.C." title="National Register of Historic Places listings in Washington, D.C.">
       National Register of Historic Places listings in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
      ; and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Washington,_D.C." title="List of museums in Washington, D.C.">
       List of museums in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg/220px-Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg/330px-Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg/440px-Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lincolnmemorial_by_dusk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Lincoln Memorial had over six million visitors in 2012.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourism2012_133-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-tourism2012-133">
          [127]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/National_Mall" title="National Mall">
       National Mall
      </a>
      is a large, open park in downtown Washington between the
      <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Memorial" title="Lincoln Memorial">
       Lincoln Memorial
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">
       United States Capitol
      </a>
      . Given its prominence, the mall is often the location of
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_protest_marches_on_Washington,_D.C." title="List of protest marches on Washington, D.C.">
       political protests
      </a>
      , concerts, festivals, and
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_inauguration" title="United States presidential inauguration">
       presidential inaugurations
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monument" title="Washington Monument">
       Washington Monument
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Pier" title="Jefferson Pier">
       Jefferson Pier
      </a>
      are near the center of the mall, south of the
      <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
       White House
      </a>
      . Also on the mall are the
      <a href="/wiki/National_World_War_II_Memorial" title="National World War II Memorial">
       National World War II Memorial
      </a>
      at the east end of the
      <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Memorial_Reflecting_Pool" title="Lincoln Memorial Reflecting Pool">
       Lincoln Memorial Reflecting Pool
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Korean_War_Veterans_Memorial" title="Korean War Veterans Memorial">
       Korean War Veterans Memorial
      </a>
      , and the Vietnam Veterans Memorial.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nama_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nama-136">
        [130]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Directly south of the mall, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidal_Basin_(District_of_Columbia)" title="Tidal Basin (District of Columbia)">
       Tidal Basin
      </a>
      features rows of Japanese cherry blossom trees that originated as gifts from the nation of Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        [131]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Memorial" title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt Memorial">
       Franklin Delano Roosevelt Memorial
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_Memorial" title="George Mason Memorial">
       George Mason Memorial
      </a>
      , Jefferson Memorial,
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr._Memorial" title="Martin Luther King Jr. Memorial">
       Martin Luther King Jr. Memorial
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_War_Memorial" title="District of Columbia War Memorial">
       District of Columbia War Memorial
      </a>
      are around the Tidal Basin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nama_136-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nama-136">
        [130]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/National_Archives_and_Records_Administration" title="National Archives and Records Administration">
       National Archives
      </a>
      houses thousands of documents important to American history including the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">
       Declaration of Independence
      </a>
      , the United States Constitution, and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">
       Bill of Rights
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        [132]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Located in three buildings on Capitol Hill, the
      <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
       Library of Congress
      </a>
      is the largest library complex in the world with a collection of over 147 million books, manuscripts, and other materials.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court_Building" title="United States Supreme Court Building">
       United States Supreme Court Building
      </a>
      was completed in 1935; before then, the court held sessions in the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Senate_Chamber" title="Old Senate Chamber">
       Old Senate Chamber
      </a>
      of the Capitol.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1181" data-file-width="1451" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg/220px-SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg/330px-SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg/440px-SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SmithsonianCastel_07120014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">
         Smithsonian Institution
        </a>
        operates 19 museums and the
        <a href="/wiki/National_Zoological_Park_(United_States)" title="National Zoological Park (United States)">
         National Zoo
        </a>
        , all free to the public.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">
       Smithsonian Institution
      </a>
      is an educational foundation chartered by Congress in 1846 that maintains most of the nation's official museums and galleries in Washington, D.C. The U.S. government partially funds the Smithsonian and its collections open to the public free of charge.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        [135]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Smithsonian's locations had a combined total of 30 million visits in 2013. The most visited museum is the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="National Museum of Natural History">
       National Museum of Natural History
      </a>
      on the National Mall.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other Smithsonian Institution museums and galleries on the mall are: the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">
       National Air and Space Museum
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_African_Art" title="National Museum of African Art">
       National Museum of African Art
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_American_History" title="National Museum of American History">
       National Museum of American History
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_American_Indian" title="National Museum of the American Indian">
       National Museum of the American Indian
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/Arthur_M._Sackler_Gallery" title="Arthur M. Sackler Gallery">
       Sackler
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Freer_Gallery_of_Art" title="Freer Gallery of Art">
       Freer
      </a>
      galleries, which both focus on Asian art and culture; the
      <a href="/wiki/Hirshhorn_Museum_and_Sculpture_Garden" title="Hirshhorn Museum and Sculpture Garden">
       Hirshhorn Museum and Sculpture Garden
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/Arts_and_Industries_Building" title="Arts and Industries Building">
       Arts and Industries Building
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/S._Dillon_Ripley_Center" title="S. Dillon Ripley Center">
       S. Dillon Ripley Center
      </a>
      ; and the
      <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution_Building" title="Smithsonian Institution Building">
       Smithsonian Institution Building
      </a>
      (also known as "The Castle"), which serves as the institution's headquarters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI_143-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SI-143">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_American_Art_Museum" title="Smithsonian American Art Museum">
       Smithsonian American Art Museum
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Portrait_Gallery_(United_States)" title="National Portrait Gallery (United States)">
       National Portrait Gallery
      </a>
      are housed in the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Patent_Office_Building" title="Old Patent Office Building">
       Old Patent Office Building
      </a>
      , near Washington's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Washington,_D.C." title="Chinatown, Washington, D.C.">
       Chinatown
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        [138]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Renwick_Gallery" title="Renwick Gallery">
       Renwick Gallery
      </a>
      is officially part of the Smithsonian American Art Museum but is in a separate building near the White House. Other Smithsonian museums and galleries include: the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anacostia_Museum" title="Anacostia Museum">
       Anacostia Community Museum
      </a>
      in Southeast Washington; the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Postal_Museum" title="National Postal Museum">
       National Postal Museum
      </a>
      near
      <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Union Station (Washington, D.C.)">
       Union Station
      </a>
      ; and the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Zoological_Park_(United_States)" title="National Zoological Park (United States)">
       National Zoo
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Woodley_Park,_Washington,_D.C." title="Woodley Park, Washington, D.C.">
       Woodley Park
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI_143-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SI-143">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Art" title="National Gallery of Art">
       National Gallery of Art
      </a>
      is on the National Mall near the Capitol and features works of American and European art. The gallery and its collections are owned by the U.S. government but are not a part of the Smithsonian Institution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        [139]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/National_Building_Museum" title="National Building Museum">
       National Building Museum
      </a>
      , which occupies the former Pension Building near
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judiciary_Square,_Washington,_D.C." title="Judiciary Square, Washington, D.C.">
       Judiciary Square
      </a>
      , was chartered by Congress and hosts exhibits on architecture, urban planning, and design.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        [140]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There are many private art museums in the District of Columbia, which house major collections and exhibits open to the public such as the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Women_in_the_Arts" title="National Museum of Women in the Arts">
       National Museum of Women in the Arts
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/Corcoran_Gallery_of_Art" title="Corcoran Gallery of Art">
       Corcoran Gallery of Art
      </a>
      , the largest private museum in Washington;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        [141]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Phillips_Collection" title="The Phillips Collection">
       The Phillips Collection
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dupont_Circle,_Washington,_D.C." title="Dupont Circle, Washington, D.C.">
       Dupont Circle
      </a>
      , the first museum of modern art in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        [142]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other private museums in Washington include the
      <a href="/wiki/Newseum" title="Newseum">
       Newseum
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/O_Street_Museum_Foundation" title="O Street Museum Foundation">
       O Street Museum Foundation
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Spy_Museum" title="International Spy Museum">
       International Spy Museum
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">
       National Geographic Society
      </a>
      Museum, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Marian_Koshland_Science_Museum" title="Marian Koshland Science Museum">
       Marian Koshland Science Museum
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum" title="United States Holocaust Memorial Museum">
       United States Holocaust Memorial Museum
      </a>
      near the National Mall maintains exhibits, documentation, and artifacts related to the Holocaust.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        [143]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">
       Arts
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theater_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Theater in Washington, D.C.">
       Theater in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Washington,_D.C." title="Music of Washington, D.C.">
       Music of Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1937" data-file-width="3118" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg/220px-Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg/330px-Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg/440px-Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_Center_at_Dusk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="John F. Kennedy Center for the Performing Arts">
         John F. Kennedy Center for the Performing Arts
        </a>
        on the Potomac River
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:True_Reformer_Building.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/True_Reformer_Building.jpg/220px-True_Reformer_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/True_Reformer_Building.jpg/330px-True_Reformer_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/True_Reformer_Building.jpg/440px-True_Reformer_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:True_Reformer_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Mural of
        <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ellington" title="Duke Ellington">
         Duke Ellington
        </a>
        on
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U_Street_Corridor" title="U Street Corridor">
         U Street
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Washington, D.C., is a national center for the arts. The
      <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="John F. Kennedy Center for the Performing Arts">
       John F. Kennedy Center for the Performing Arts
      </a>
      is home to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Symphony_Orchestra_(United_States)" title="National Symphony Orchestra (United States)">
       National Symphony Orchestra
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_National_Opera" title="Washington National Opera">
       Washington National Opera
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Ballet" title="Washington Ballet">
       Washington Ballet
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">
       Kennedy Center Honors
      </a>
      are awarded each year to those in the performing arts who have contributed greatly to the cultural life of the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        [144]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The historic
      <a href="/wiki/Ford%27s_Theatre" title="Ford's Theatre">
       Ford's Theatre
      </a>
      , site of the assassination of President
      <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">
       Abraham Lincoln
      </a>
      , continues to operate as a functioning performance space as well as museum.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        [145]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Marine_Barracks,_Washington,_D.C." title="Marine Barracks, Washington, D.C.">
       Marine Barracks
      </a>
      near
      <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Hill" title="Capitol Hill">
       Capitol Hill
      </a>
      houses the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Band" title="United States Marine Band">
       United States Marine Band
      </a>
      ; founded in 1798, it is the country's oldest professional musical organization.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        [146]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/American_march_music" title="American march music">
       American march composer
      </a>
      and Washington-native
      <a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Sousa" title="John Philip Sousa">
       John Philip Sousa
      </a>
      led the Marine Band from 1880 until 1892.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        [147]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Founded in 1925, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_Band" title="United States Navy Band">
       United States Navy Band
      </a>
      has its headquarters at the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Navy_Yard" title="Washington Navy Yard">
       Washington Navy Yard
      </a>
      and performs at official events and public concerts around the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        [148]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Washington has a strong local theater tradition. Founded in 1950,
      <a href="/wiki/Arena_Stage" title="Arena Stage">
       Arena Stage
      </a>
      achieved national attention and spurred growth in the city's independent theater movement that now includes organizations such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_Theatre_Company" title="Shakespeare Theatre Company">
       Shakespeare Theatre Company
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Woolly_Mammoth_Theatre_Company" title="Woolly Mammoth Theatre Company">
       Woolly Mammoth Theatre Company
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_Theatre" title="Studio Theatre">
       Studio Theatre
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        [149]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Arena Stage opened its newly renovated home in the city's emerging
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southwest_Waterfront,_Washington,_D.C." title="Southwest Waterfront, Washington, D.C.">
       Southwest waterfront area
      </a>
      in 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        [150]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The GALA Hispanic Theatre, now housed in the historic
      <a href="/wiki/Tivoli_Theatre_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Tivoli Theatre (Washington, D.C.)">
       Tivoli Theatre
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Heights_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Columbia Heights (Washington, D.C.)">
       Columbia Heights
      </a>
      , was founded in 1976 and is a National Center for the Latino Performing Arts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        [151]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U_Street_Corridor" title="U Street Corridor">
       U Street Corridor
      </a>
      in Northwest D.C., known as "Washington's Black Broadway", is home to institutions like the
      <a href="/wiki/Howard_Theatre" title="Howard Theatre">
       Howard Theatre
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Caverns" title="Bohemian Caverns">
       Bohemian Caverns
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Theatre_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Lincoln Theatre (Washington, D.C.)">
       Lincoln Theatre
      </a>
      , which hosted music legends such as Washington-native
      <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ellington" title="Duke Ellington">
       Duke Ellington
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Coltrane" title="John Coltrane">
       John Coltrane
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Miles_Davis" title="Miles Davis">
       Miles Davis
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ustreet_158-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ustreet-158">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Washington has its own native music genre called
      <a href="/wiki/Go-go" title="Go-go">
       go-go
      </a>
      ; a post-funk, percussion-driven flavor of rhythm and blues that was popularized in the late 1970s by D.C. band leader
      <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Brown" title="Chuck Brown">
       Chuck Brown
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        [153]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The District is an important center for
      <a href="/wiki/Indie_music_scene" title="Indie music scene">
       indie culture and music
      </a>
      in the United States. The label
      <a href="/wiki/Dischord_Records" title="Dischord Records">
       Dischord Records
      </a>
      , formed by
      <a href="/wiki/Ian_MacKaye" title="Ian MacKaye">
       Ian MacKaye
      </a>
      , was one of the most crucial independent labels in the genesis of 1980s punk and eventually indie rock in the 1990s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        [154]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Modern
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">
       alternative
      </a>
      and indie music venues like
      <a href="/wiki/Black_Cat_(Washington,_D.C._nightclub)" title="Black Cat (Washington, D.C. nightclub)">
       The Black Cat
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/9:30_Club" title="9:30 Club">
       9:30 Club
      </a>
      bring popular acts to the U Street area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        [155]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
       Sports
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Sports in Washington, D.C.">
       Sports in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Verizon_Center.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Verizon_Center.jpg/220px-Verizon_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Verizon_Center.jpg/330px-Verizon_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Verizon_Center.jpg/440px-Verizon_Center.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Verizon_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Center" title="Verizon Center">
         Verizon Center
        </a>
        in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Washington,_D.C." title="Chinatown, Washington, D.C.">
         Chinatown
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Washington is one of 12 cities in the United States with teams
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._cities_with_teams_from_four_major_sports" title="U.S. cities with teams from four major sports">
       from all four major professional men's sports
      </a>
      and is home to one major professional women's team. The
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wizards" title="Washington Wizards">
       Washington Wizards
      </a>
      (National Basketball Association), the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Capitals" title="Washington Capitals">
       Washington Capitals
      </a>
      (National Hockey League), and the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Mystics" title="Washington Mystics">
       Washington Mystics
      </a>
      (Women's National Basketball Association), play at the
      <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Center" title="Verizon Center">
       Verizon Center
      </a>
      in Chinatown.
      <a href="/wiki/Nationals_Park" title="Nationals Park">
       Nationals Park
      </a>
      , which opened in Southeast D.C. in 2008, is home to the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">
       Washington Nationals
      </a>
      (Major League Baseball).
      <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">
       D.C. United
      </a>
      (Major League Soccer) plays at
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy_Memorial_Stadium" title="Robert F. Kennedy Memorial Stadium">
       RFK Stadium
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">
       Washington Redskins
      </a>
      (National Football League) play at nearby
      <a href="/wiki/FedExField" title="FedExField">
       FedExField
      </a>
      in Landover, Maryland.
     </p>
     <p>
      Current D.C. teams have won a combined ten professional league championships: the Washington Redskins have won five;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        [156]
       </a>
      </sup>
      D.C. United has won four;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        [157]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the Washington Wizards (then the Washington Bullets) have won a single championship.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        [158]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Other professional and semi-professional teams in Washington include: the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Kastles" title="Washington Kastles">
       Washington Kastles
      </a>
      (World TeamTennis); the
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_D.C._Slayers" title="Washington D.C. Slayers">
       Washington D.C. Slayers
      </a>
      (USA Rugby League); the Baltimore Washington Eagles (U.S. Australian Football League); the
      <a href="/wiki/D.C._Divas" title="D.C. Divas">
       D.C. Divas
      </a>
      (Independent Women's Football League); and the
      <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Athletic_Club_RFC" title="Potomac Athletic Club RFC">
       Potomac Athletic Club RFC
      </a>
      (Rugby Super League). The
      <a href="/wiki/William_H.G._FitzGerald_Tennis_Center" title="William H.G. FitzGerald Tennis Center">
       William H.G. FitzGerald Tennis Center
      </a>
      in Rock Creek Park hosts the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citi_Open" title="Citi Open">
       Citi Open
      </a>
      . Washington is also home to two major annual marathon races: the
      <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Marathon" title="Marine Corps Marathon">
       Marine Corps Marathon
      </a>
      , which is held every autumn, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_%27n%27_Roll_USA_Marathon" title="Rock 'n' Roll USA Marathon">
       Rock 'n' Roll USA Marathon
      </a>
      held in the spring. The Marine Corps Marathon began in 1976 and is sometimes called "The People's Marathon" because it is the largest marathon that does not offer prize money to participants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        [159]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The District's four
      <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
       NCAA
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">
       Division I
      </a>
      teams,
      <a href="/wiki/American_Eagles" title="American Eagles">
       American Eagles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Colonials" title="George Washington Colonials">
       George Washington Colonials
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Hoyas" title="Georgetown Hoyas">
       Georgetown Hoyas
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Howard_Bison_and_Lady_Bison" title="Howard Bison and Lady Bison">
       Howard Bison and Lady Bison
      </a>
      , have a broad following. The
      <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball" title="Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball">
       Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball
      </a>
      team is the most notable and also plays at the Verizon Center. From 2008 to 2012, the District hosted an annual
      <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">
       college football
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">
       bowl game
      </a>
      at RFK Stadium, called the
      <a href="/wiki/Military_Bowl" title="Military Bowl">
       Military Bowl
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        [160]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The D.C. area is home to one regional sports television network,
      <a href="/wiki/Comcast_SportsNet" title="Comcast SportsNet">
       Comcast SportsNet
      </a>
      (CSN), based in Bethesda, Maryland.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
       Media
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Media in Washington, D.C.">
       Media in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Washington,_D.C." title="List of newspapers in Washington, D.C.">
       List of newspapers in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_shows_set_in_Washington,_D.C." title="List of television shows set in Washington, D.C.">
       List of television shows set in Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row,_1874.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="919" data-file-width="1619" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row%2C_1874.jpg/220px-Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row%2C_1874.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row%2C_1874.jpg/330px-Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row%2C_1874.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row%2C_1874.jpg/440px-Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row%2C_1874.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Washington_DC_Newspaper_Row,_1874.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Washington's Newspaper Row on
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Avenue_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Pennsylvania Avenue (Washington, D.C.)">
         Pennsylvania Avenue
        </a>
        in 1874
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Washington, D.C. is a prominent center for national and international media.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">
        The Washington Post
       </a>
      </i>
      , founded in 1877, is the oldest and most-read local daily newspaper in Washington.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapo_167-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wapo-167">
        [161]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is probably most notable for its coverage of national and international politics and for exposing the
      <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">
       Watergate scandal
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        [162]
       </a>
      </sup>
      "The Post", as it is popularly called, had the sixth-highest readership of all news dailies in the country in 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        [163]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post_Company" title="The Washington Post Company">
       The Washington Post Company
      </a>
      also publishesa daily free commuter newspaper called the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Express_(Washington,_D.C._newspaper)" title="Express (Washington, D.C. newspaper)">
        Express
       </a>
      </i>
      , which summarizes events, sports and entertainment, as well as the Spanish-language paper
      <i>
       El Tiempo Latino
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Another popular local daily is
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Times" title="The Washington Times">
        The Washington Times
       </a>
      </i>
      , the city's second general interest broadsheet and also an influential paper in political circles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        [164]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_newspaper" title="Alternative newspaper">
       alternative weekly
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_City_Paper" title="Washington City Paper">
        Washington City Paper
       </a>
      </i>
      also have substantial readership in the Washington area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        [165]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        [166]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some community and specialty papers focus on neighborhood and cultural issues, including the weekly
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Blade" title="Washington Blade">
        Washington Blade
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Metro_Weekly" title="Metro Weekly">
        Metro Weekly
       </a>
      </i>
      , which focus on LGBT issues; the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Informer" title="Washington Informer">
        Washington Informer
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Afro_American" title="The Washington Afro American">
        The Washington Afro American
       </a>
      </i>
      , which highlight topics of interest to the black community; and neighborhood newspapers published by
      <a href="/wiki/The_Current_Newspapers" title="The Current Newspapers">
       The Current Newspapers
      </a>
      .
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Quarterly" title="Congressional Quarterly">
        Congressional Quarterly
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hill_(newspaper)" title="The Hill (newspaper)">
        The Hill
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Politico_(newspaper)" title="Politico (newspaper)">
        Politico
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Roll_Call" title="Roll Call">
        Roll Call
       </a>
      </i>
      newspapers focus exclusively on issues related to Congress and the federal government. Other publications based in Washington include the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">
        National Geographic
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine and political publications such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Examiner" title="The Washington Examiner">
        The Washington Examiner
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_New_Republic" title="The New Republic">
       The New Republic
      </a>
      <i>
       and
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">
       Washington Monthly
      </a>
      <i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
        <a href="#cite_note-173">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </i>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Washington Metropolitan Area is the ninth-largest television media market in the nation, with two million homes, approximately 2% of the country's population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        [168]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several media companies and cable television channels have their headquarters in the area, including
      <a href="/wiki/C-SPAN" title="C-SPAN">
       C-SPAN
      </a>
      ;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" title="Black Entertainment Television">
       Black Entertainment Television
      </a>
      (BET);
      <a href="/wiki/Radio_One_(company)" title="Radio One (company)">
       Radio One
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Channel" title="National Geographic Channel">
       National Geographic Channel
      </a>
      ;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Networks" title="Smithsonian Networks">
       Smithsonian Networks
      </a>
      ;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">
       National Public Radio
      </a>
      (NPR);
      <a href="/wiki/Travel_Channel" title="Travel Channel">
       Travel Channel
      </a>
      (in
      <a href="/wiki/Chevy_Chase,_Maryland" title="Chevy Chase, Maryland">
       Chevy Chase, Maryland
      </a>
      );
      <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">
       Discovery Communications
      </a>
      (in
      <a href="/wiki/Silver_Spring,_Maryland" title="Silver Spring, Maryland">
       Silver Spring, Maryland
      </a>
      ); and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">
       Public Broadcasting Service
      </a>
      (PBS) (in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" title="Arlington, Virginia">
       Arlington, Virginia
      </a>
      ). The headquarters of
      <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">
       Voice of America
      </a>
      , the U.S. government's international news service, is near the Capitol in Southwest Washington.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        [169]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
       Government and politics
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Washington,_D.C." title="Government of Washington, D.C.">
       Government of Washington, D.C.
      </a>
     </div>
